    Lab 4: Implementing an Idea¶

    Does it say “notebook is read only” in a button on your toolbar? Is the “save” button greyed out?
    If you want to be able to run this notebook and save your work, you need to copy it to your user directory. In the file browser on the left (click the folder icon), right click this notebook file (lab-1.ipynb), copy it, then navigate to your user home directory, and right click and choose paste. Then open that copy instead of the read-only copy, and you’ll be good to go.

    import altair as alt
import pandas as pd

import passengersim as pax

pax.versions()

    passengersim 0.80
passengersim.core 0.80

    In this lab, we will look at implementing a new idea in PassengerSim. Or, we will pretend our idea is “new”, but actually we’ll borrow someone else’s existing idea. We will loosely follow an idea previously explored by the PODS consortium: “Modeling the Effects of User Influence in Revenue Management”, Eric Hao, May 2013

    The user compares current loads on a leg at a time frame to a historical sample (or set of samples).

    • If the current load is too low, adjust the forecast to be lower, decreasing seat protection in order to accept more bookings.

    • If the current load is too high, adjust forecast to be higher, increasing seat protection to value high fare passengers.

    In previous PODS work, this idea was called “user influence”, or “dynamic user influence” (DUI).
    For this work, we want to rename the idea, partly because “DUI” means something else to many people, but moreso to remove some ambiguity, as the “user” here doesn’t actually refer to the PassengerSim user, but rather to a theoretical RM analyst who would be using some tool to tinker with the RM system while it is running. So we will call this idea a “heuristic adjustment”.

    Note this lab is not meant as any kind of proof for whether this idea is good or bad, but rather as a technical guide for how to work with PassengerSim to implement and test an idea. We selected this idea to explore because it will exercise two different sides of using PassengerSim: tinkering with outputs to create a bespoke analysis of simulation results, and tinkering with the inputs and algorithms to change how the simulation runs.

    To get started, we’ll load the config for the standard 3MKT demo model to work with.

    cfg = pax.Config.from_yaml(pax.demo_network("3MKT/DEMO"))

    The idea of what we want to do has two parts:

    • Get some idea of what the range of “normal” booked load factor looks like over the booking curve.

    • While running a simulation, compare the current booked load factor at any point to the “normal” range, and apply an intervention if we are running too hot or too cold.

    You could think about doing all of this endogenously within the simulation, but
    for this lab, we will do the first step by making a static analysis of simulation results, and then provide those curves back to the simultion as an exogenous set of “normal” curves. In some respects this is “cheating” by using too much knowledge, but since this lab is about learning the mechanics of PassengerSim, we’ll allow it.

    So, Step 1 is to run the simulation and collect the data we need. We need to use a callback function to collect the base data we want to use for making the upper and lower bound curves. A callback function gets called at regular intervals during the simulation (e.g. daily) and allows us to interrogate the simulation and store whatever we want.

    def collect_blf_detail(sim: pax.Simulation, days_prior: int) -> dict | None:
    """A daily callback function to collect booked load factor for all legs."""
    if sim.eng.sample < sim.eng.burn_samples:
        # don't collect data during burn period
        return None
    # create a dictionary to store the booked load factor for each leg
    out = {}
    # iterate over all legs in the simulation engine,
    # and collect the current booked load factor
    for leg in sim.eng.legs:
        key = leg.leg_id
        out[f"leg-{key}"] = leg.sold / leg.capacity
    # return the value, which will be end up as "callback_data" in the results
    return out

    Now we need to run the simulation with this callback to collect some data.

    sim = pax.Simulation(cfg)
sim.daily_callback(collect_blf_detail)
summary = sim.run()

    

    Task Completed after 2.48 seconds

    

    

    

    We got a bunch of source data now.  That callback function ran once every simulated day,
and it gave us a dictionary of stored values.

    Let’s manipulate the data to be more useful.  Nothing that’s special about PassengerSim here,
just run-of-the-mill data analysis with Python and Pandas.
    

    

    

    df = pd.DataFrame(summary.callback_data.daily)

# convert from wide to long format
df = df.melt(id_vars=["trial", "sample", "days_prior"], var_name="leg", value_name="blf")

# extract leg_id from leg column and convert to int
df["leg"] = df["leg"].str.replace("leg-", "").astype(int)

    With relatively minimal effort, we have a usable pandas.DataFrame of data.  We can
do whatever regular analysis we like, using totally standard Python tools. Since this
part is all plain-vanilla data analyis, AI can do a pretty good job helping. For
example, we can ask our AI assistant:
    

    

    Take leg id 101 from the data, select every 30th sample day from trial number 1,
and plot the selected trajectories of blf by days prior in an altair figure.
    

    

    And we get might get something like this:
    

    

    

    leg_101_data = df[(df["leg"] == 101) & (df["trial"] == 1) & (df["sample"] % 30 == 0)].copy()

chart_101 = (
    alt.Chart(leg_101_data)
    .mark_line()
    .encode(
        x=alt.X("days_prior:Q", scale=alt.Scale(domain=(63, 0)), title="Days Prior to Departure"),
        y=alt.Y("blf:Q", title="Booked Load Factor (blf)"),
        color=alt.Color("sample:N", title="Sample"),
        tooltip=["trial", "sample", "days_prior", "blf"],
    )
    .properties(title="Leg 101 BLF Trajectories (Trial 1, Every 30th Sample)")
    .interactive()
)

    limits = (0.1, 0.9)

    Let’s look at the bounds we found:
    

    

    

    chart = (
    alt.Chart(bounds)

    The bounds are very similar for all the BOS-ORD legs, and also for all the ORD-LAX legs.
This is not surprising, the network is perfectly symmetric.
    

    Let’s use tags to group legs together, so we can use common booked load factor curves.
We can attach tags to each leg config, and those tags will also be available on the
the simulation legs.
    

    In this example we write tags based only on O and D, and only for AL1, but we could tag
any legs based on any attribute we like.
    

    

    

    for leg in cfg.legs:
    if leg.carrier == "AL1":
        if leg.orig == "BOS" and leg.dest == "ORD":
            leg.tags["BLF_Curve"] = "BOSTONtoCHICAGO"
        if leg.orig == "ORD" and leg.dest == "LAX":
            leg.tags["BLF_Curve"] = "CHICAGOtoLA"

    

    

    

    

    We can create a mapping for all the leg id’s that have a “BLF_Curve” tag.
    

    

    

    tag_map = {leg.leg_id: tag for leg in cfg.legs if (tag := leg.tags.get("BLF_Curve"))}
tag_map

    

    

    

    

    {101: 'BOSTONtoCHICAGO',
 102: 'BOSTONtoCHICAGO',
 111: 'CHICAGOtoLA',
 112: 'CHICAGOtoLA'}

    

    

    

    

    Then we can use that mapping to compute the booked load factor lower and upper bound curves, aggregated by those tags.
    

    

    

    df["leg_tag"] = df["leg"].apply(tag_map.get)

bounds = pd.concat(
    [
        df.groupby(["leg_tag", "days_prior"])["blf"].quantile(limits[0]).rename("lower_bound"),
        df.groupby(["leg_tag", "days_prior"])["blf"].quantile(limits[1]).rename("upper_bound"),
    ],
    axis=1,
).reset_index()

bounds

    We can convert the bounds dataframe to a nested dictionary, to make looking up values relatively fast.
We want it to be fast because we’re going to do it a lot.
    

    

    

    def nest_dict(df: pd.DataFrame) -> dict:
    assert isinstance(df.index, pd.MultiIndex), "DataFrame index must be a MultiIndex"
    flat_dict = df.to_dict(orient="index")
    result = {}
    for key, value in flat_dict.items():
        target = result
        # Traverse all keys but the last one
        for k in key[:-1]:
            target = target.setdefault(k, {})
        # Assign the final value
        target[key[-1]] = value
    return result


bounds_dict = nest_dict(bounds.set_index(["leg_tag", "days_prior"]))
bounds_dict

    from passengersim.rm import RmAction

SECONDS_PER_DAY = 24 * 60 * 60


class BookedLoadFactor(RmAction):
    frequency = "daily"

    def __init__(
        self,
        *,
        carrier: str,
        minimum_sample: int = 10,
        cfg: pax.Config | None = None,
        adjustment_multiplier: float = 1.1,
        min_days_between_actions: int = 7,
    ):
        """
        Apply an adjustment to leg forecasted demand when the bookings are atypical.

        Parameters
        ----------
        carrier : str
            Apply the adjustment only to legs for this carrier.
        minimum_sample : int
            Do not apply any adjustment until at least this many samples have
            been simulated.
        cfg : pax.Config | None
            The configuration object for the simulation.  The booked load factor
            curves will be stored in the `other_controls` section of this config.
        adjustment_multiplier : float, default 1.1
            The multiplier to apply to demand when bookings exceed the upper bound
            curve of the booked load factor range. The inverse of this multiplier
            will be applied when bookings fail to meet the lower bound curve.
        """
        super().__init__(carrier=carrier, minimum_sample=minimum_sample, cfg=cfg)

        self.hot_multiplier = adjustment_multiplier
        """The multiplier to apply when bookings exceed the upper bound."""

        self.cold_multiplier = 1.0 / adjustment_multiplier
        """The multiplier to apply when bookings fail to meet the lower bound."""

        self.latest_update_times = {}
        """Track the last time that an adjustment was applied to each leg."""

        self.min_days_between_actions = min_days_between_actions
        """Minimum wait period before applying another demand adjustment."""

    def reset(self, sim: pax.Simulation):
        """Clear all forecast multipliers for this carrier.

        This is typically done at the end of a simulation sample (i.e. at
        departure).
        """
        self.latest_update_times.clear()
        for leg in sim.eng.legs.set_filters(carrier=self.carrier):
            for bucket in leg.buckets:
                del bucket.forecast_multiplier

    def run(self, sim: pax.Simulation, days_prior: int):
        """Run this action for the simulation and given days prior to departure."""
        if sim.eng.sample < self.minimum_sample:
            return

        # At the end of each sample, set all multipliers back to zero.
        if days_prior == 0:
            self.reset(sim)
            return

        # any leg that has been adjusted more recently than a cutoff time will be skipped
        current_time = sim.eng.last_event_time
        cutoff_time = current_time - self.min_days_between_actions * SECONDS_PER_DAY

        for leg in sim.eng.legs.set_filters(carrier=self.carrier):
            # for each leg, find the name of the appropriate BLF curve
            leg_blf_curve = leg.tags.get("BLF_Curve")
            # if there is no BLF curve tag, apply no adjustment
            if leg_blf_curve is None:
                continue
            # if this leg has been adjusted more recently than the cutoff time, skip it
            if self.latest_update_times.get(leg.leg_id, 0) > cutoff_time:
                continue
            # find the upper and lower bounds for this leg and days_prior
            ub = bounds_dict[leg_blf_curve][days_prior]["upper_bound"]
            lb = bounds_dict[leg_blf_curve][days_prior]["lower_bound"]
            # calculate the current booked load factor for this leg
            leg_booked = leg.sold / leg.capacity
            # if the leg is too hot or too cold, apply the appropriate adjustment
            # and record the time of this adjustment in latest_update_times
            if leg_booked > ub:
                for bucket in leg.buckets:
                    bucket.forecast_multiplier *= self.hot_multiplier
                self.latest_update_times[leg.leg_id] = current_time
            elif leg_booked < lb:
                for bucket in leg.buckets:
                    bucket.forecast_multiplier *= self.cold_multiplier
                self.latest_update_times[leg.leg_id] = current_time

    

    

    

    

    

    

    from passengersim.rm.emsr import ExpectedMarginalSeatRevenue
from passengersim.rm.standard_forecasting import StandardLegForecast
from passengersim.rm.systems import RmSys, register_rm_system
from passengersim.rm.untruncation import LegUntruncation


@register_rm_system
class EX(RmSys):
    availability_control = "leg"
    """This RM system uses leg-level class allocation availability controls."""

    actions = [
        LegUntruncation,
        StandardLegForecast,
        BookedLoadFactor,
        ExpectedMarginalSeatRevenue,
    ]

    

    

    

    

    

    

    cfg.carriers.AL1.rm_system = "EX"

    

    

    

    

    

    

    sim2 = pax.Simulation(cfg)
summary2 = sim2.run()
